Love you and wish you loved me back.

Want our family back.

Want you back.

Hate seeing our daughter cry.

Way more than a kid should ever know about their parents.

January, 2011.

And they had just spent the day trekking through snow and sleet to get everything moved into their new home. The one they owned. Agatha was pretty sure that was a first for a Harkness woman. Evanora just bounced from apartment to apartment until they evicted her ass, and subsequently, Agatha’s too.

They had gotten it at a bargain, the townhome being a little rough around the edges. Meaning, it was old and in desperate need of several thousand updates and repairs. Jen and Alice didn’t keep the old house once Rio and Agatha announced they had found a place, instead they opted to get a swanky apartment near the hospital.

And maybe that life was with a beautiful woman, one who was happy to ease her suffering. Maybe that life was with Wanda, and maybe it was good.

Either way–

Agatha was finished playing with fire.

Their daughter glanced up from the screen. “No, mami, c’mon. We’re watching Twilight.”

Rio’s brows furrowed. “The vampire movie?”

“The whole saga.” Agatha corrected.

“Not if you watch it ironically.” Their daughter yawned.

So, that’s how they spent the rest of the morning into the afternoon. Agatha didn't think the three of them would ever do something like this again, waste a day with one another. But having her ex wife there wasn't terrible. As they moved on from movie to movie, the little jokes and comments became more and more common.

“Why does the blond one look like that?” Rio asked during New Moon.

“Who? Jasper?” Agatha peered over.

“Yeah. That guy.”

“Unsolved mystery.” Their daughter answered. “Dude looks constipated.”

The day morphed, Nicky’s bed becoming an island of tissues and meds, both her ex and daughter drifting in and out of sleep. After Eclipse, they all changed into pjs, Agatha loaning Rio some sweatpants and a Red Sox hoodie that Agatha still wore often even though it technically belonged to her ex.

It was about half way through Breaking Dawn when both Rio and Nicky had passed out, her daughter drooling on her chest the same way Rio was currently drooling on a pillow. The sun had set already and Agatha was eerily calm, letting herself close her eyes and doze off as before Bella gave birth. She was actually tired, but she also didn’t need to watch the labor and delivery scene.

Her eyes only opened at a loud noise from the laptop, she had turned over in her sleep, an arm slung over her waist. She roused, blinking a few times and peeking down at what she assumed was her daughter’s limb. Her face fell as she recognized the hand that was limp against her abdomen, as she recognized that ring.

She flipped over, too quickly, causing Rio next to her to wake up. Amber eyes came into focus, her ex wife pulling her arm back as though it would be sliced off for touching Agatha.

“Shit.” Rio whispered.

Agatha looked around but didn’t get up. “Where’s Nicky?”

Her ex paused the movie and slumped back against the pillow. “No clue.”

She should get up, she should put distance between them because right now they were mere inches apart. “I never ordered ginger ale.”

“Probably for the better, that shit is awful.”

Agatha grinned, looking over Rio’s shoulder at the clock. “I should probably make dinner. You know, soup or something…”

And Rio’s lips curled up. “Okay.”

Yet, Agatha still didn’t move.

They weren’t touching.

They weren’t doing anything but talking.

Nothing untoward was happening.

She scooted in, just fractionally, just to get comfortable.

Rio mirrored her and moved in too, their knees brushing one another.

“Did,” Rio swallowed. “Did you want me to head out?”

Her gaze naturally followed the slope of her ex wife’s nose, down to her cupid’s bow, stopping at her lips. Rio was sick, her breath could not be appealing now more than ever, but the day had been so good and nostalgia is an effective drug.

“No.” She responded, tilting her face and letting the tip of her nose graze Rio’s.

“I thought you wanted to stop.”

“We’re not doing anything.”

“This feels like something.”

Agatha felt Rio’s hand fall back to her waist, just resting, not gripping. “So, we should find Nicky?” She offered as a way out for the both of them.

“If you think we should.”

They should, they definitely should.

“I-”

Agatha was cut off by a knock on the front door downstairs, pulling away like she was escaping a fugue state. She scrambled off their daughter’s bed for fucks sake, bolting away and down to the first floor. She ignored the phantom sensation of Rio’s fingers as she opened the door, a cold blast of December air hitting her body. Just as effective as ice water being dumped over her frayed nerves.

Her eyes landed on Wanda on her front step, holding up a case of ginger ale. “Figured you could use this.”

Agatha blinked. “Wh- Wanda, what?”

Her girlfriend brushed past her. “I got your text that Nicky was sick, so after work I stopped at the store.”

Yeah, Agatha had texted her this morning, having abandoned her phone after all three of them got back home. “That’s- that’s really sweet of you. You didn’t have to do that.”

“I wanted to.” Wanda smiled. “Plus, I need the brownie points.”

Her daughter turned a corner from the kitchen, a sleeve of Saltines in her hand as she was drowning in a Mass Gen hoodie. Her girlfriend looked at Nicky, giving a wave. “Hey Nic, feeling any better?”

Her daughter squinted her eyes, stopping mid chew to scowl before audibly hissing at the woman in their foyer.

“What the fuck?” Wanda murmured as Nicky kept on walking.

Agatha sighed. “It’s been a day.”

“Yeah–”

“Wanda?” Rio spoke, languidly coming down the stairs, wrapped up in that throw blanket again.

Her girlfriend looked at her ex wife then back to Agatha. “Rio’s here?”

“Well, Nicky got her sick and then she couldn’t drive herself home from the hospital, so I gave her a ride…” Agatha rambled. “It just made sense for them to be sick in the same place.”

Wanda cocked her head. “Right.”

“Believe me, I’ve been surrounded by vomit all day.” She quipped. “Hardly something I planned.”

Her girlfriend nodded, though clearly unconvinced. She held out the ginger ale. “Well, I’ll leave you guys to it.”

“Wanda–”

“It’s fine.” Wanda dismissed, leaving and closing the door behind her.

“Fuck.” Agatha set down the soda, grabbing a coat and her snow boots to follow. She didn’t miss the way her ex watched as she did so. She slammed the door behind her, doing a half jog to catch up to her girlfriend down the walkway. “Wanda.”

“I said it’s fine.” Wanda repeated as she stopped. “I just would’ve appreciated the heads up.”

“Hon, it was a last minute thing. I didn’t invite her, Nicky did.”

She chose not to point out that she also hadn’t invited Wanda either, probably wouldn’t help the situation.

“Agatha.” Her girlfriend blew out a breath. “Do you understand how I feel? I know how your daughter sees me, I know how your ex sees me. And I’ve been patient, I’ve brushed it off. But I need you to be honest with me.”

“I have been.” She lied, her breath visible beneath the street lamps.

“I see that way Rio looks at you.” Wanda bitterly chuckled. “Am I wasting my time here? Because…I thought we were really going somewhere. It’s been almost a year, I’m serious about you.”

“What? No. Wanda,” She took a step forward, curling her fingers around the hem of Wanda’s jacket. “I’m with you. My ex wife is…she’s always going to be in my life but I’m with you.”

“So you can honestly say that you don’t feel anything for her?” Wanda tilted her head.

And Agatha had to be smart here, because today was a glitch.

Today, Nicky liked her. And today was nice. But tomorrow? Tomorrow she’d go back to being the reason why Rio lived on a different street. Tomorrow she’d go back to being the reason Nicky had her life scattered between two homes. Tomorrow she’d go back to being the reason why they weren’t a family anymore.

But Wanda was the same as she was yesterday, today, and how she’d be tomorrow. And Agatha needed that, the consistency. It’s not that she didn’t like Wanda, she just needed to redirect her focus onto her and away from Rio.

“I can honestly say, I don’t want her.” Agatha lied again. “I want you.”

Agatha didn’t want to want Rio.

Agatha wanted to want Wanda.

“You mean that?”

“I do.”

And she really hoped she would someday.

Her and Rio weren’t sustainable, not after everything. Agatha needed to get her shit together for the sake of her daughter and her relationship with Wanda. A clear boundary drawn with her ex. She needed Rio as a co-parent, not a back up whenever she felt like it. She needed Wanda as a partner, not someone to cry to when she felt sad.

Agatha leaned in. “I haven’t been fair to you, and I’ll be better about it. I should’ve told you Rio was here, but Wanda, I swear nothing happened.”

Which was true.

They hadn’t kissed.

There had been no adultery of any kind.

“Thank you.” Her girlfriend breathed out in relief. “I know I must sound insane-”

“It’s okay.” Agatha pulled her in, giving her a quick kiss.

Wanda wrapped her arms around Agatha’s shoulders, kissing her back. “Can I ask you something?”

“Sure.”

“What the fuck was the hissing about?”

Chapter End Notes

well...at least everyone was happy for like two minutes

“You wanna pick which flowers we give to mama?” Rio sneakily asked her daughter as they gardened together. Well, Rio gardened, Nicky toddled around in rainboots, overalls, and a bucket hat because Agatha was worried about her face getting burnt.

“Yeah!” Nicky squealed, her little legs carrying her around to different bushels of flowers.

Rio watched with a lazy grin as her three year old fisted her hand around stems and yanked them free. She chuckled to herself, crouching down with a pair of cutters and helping to sever the stems of the azaleas. “Good choice, princesa.”

May, 2016.

Nicky giggled, jumping up and down, braids jostling as she ran to a different plant. Rio diligently followed, repeating the same motions of cutting the stems so Nicky could hold the growing bouquet.

“Do you know why we give mama flowers?”

Her daughter pursed her lips in confusion, shaking her head. “No.”

“Because she’s pretty and deserves pretty flowers, right?” Rio answered, lightly poking Nicky’s stomach to make her daughter laugh again.

“Bonita!” Nicky said, her brain making the connection. She wasn’t as fluent as Rio would like, but was getting better each day.

But, it doesn’t feel…impossible this time? I don’t think I've fully forgiven you, and I don’t know how I’ll get there. But I want to try.”

Agatha had never asked, and couldn't bring herself to for a long time.

Her wife pulled her in, strong arms encircling her, tenderly whispering “It’s okay, baby. It’s okay.” over and over.

What made a child loved? The hours spent in agony over their wellbeing? The stress and anxiety about the milestones? The support and encouragement that was bestowed unconditionally? The willingness to rip your chest cavity open, the offering and burial of your own heart if it meant your child would be okay? What made a child loved? Did Agatha do enough? Could she have done more? Did she let Alex down? Did she let Nicky down? Is she letting Nicky down? Had she spent so much of her energy on the child that passed, she disjointed her relationship with the one living?

What made a child loved?

“Then why does it never feel like enough?” Why did Agatha never feel like enough?

Rio’s response was watery, fractured and tattered. “I wish I had an answer for you.”

The silence fell easily, a piece of silk clinging to everything laid beneath. It wasn’t bad, holding one another with no solution in sight. Because they didn’t have to figure out every answer today, they had time. For the first time in six years, Agatha and Rio could breathe. If the cuts were superficial or down to the fucking bone, if the wounds needed air to breathe or tending to close.

They both agreed that it would be important to spend the night separate, they couldn’t just fall back into a relationship. “Better than me, I’d block the bitch and pawn it.”

Agatha chuckled. “Let’s go.”

“Are you going to tell Nicky?” Agatha asked, heater on full blast. “Not that you have to if you’re not ready.”

Rio didn’t seem worried, grinning. “Yeah, I think she’ll take it well. Now that you know, it’s slightly less…”

“Scary?”

“I was going to say petrifying, but yeah.”

“Are you going to be okay being alone?”

“Are you?”

No.

“I’ve survived this long, haven’t I?”

“We both have.” Rio said, leaning in for a kiss.

She shot a hand up, stopping them. “What if Melina sees?”

“Mmmmh.” Rio hummed, dramatically checking to make sure if the coast was clear. “Think we’re good. Also we’re two consenting adults-”

She got home around 1PM, texting Rio before throwing herself into the task of actually shoveling the walkway. Her phone rang, Wanda’s ID on the screen, she declined the call. Agatha would wait until she was back in town tomorrow before saying something. The air was beyond frigid, but as the sun finally broke through the clouds and beamed down, she was at peace. Not because of Rio, but the things that had been left unsaid were out in the open, and that was farther than she’d ever thought she’d be.

Agatha finished the walk and driveway after an hour and some change, half assing the job enough that it was close to done. She minimally fed herself, stripping off her jacket and tossing the ring onto the entryway table as she went upstairs to take a bath. Her body was covered in sweat from shoveling and her body was aching from the manual labor and the night prior.

She’d never been more tired or satisfied in years, the mental load taxing but strangely rewarding. She stewed in the water until it went cold, eyes closed and heart calm. The grief had a light at the end of the tunnel, it was a keyhole, but it was there. Her wife texted her intermittently, not suffocating, not detached, a good balance. When the sun set and the house went ominously quiet, Agatha stood at the end of the hall in front of Alex’s door.

Agatha’s hand rested on the knob, metal latch retracting and letting the door creak wide open. She stood at the door frame, arms crossed and holding herself. Eyes scanning the space. She blew out a short breath, placing one foot across the threshold. Agatha froze, waiting. Almost as if she expected something to happen, someone to smite her down upon entry.

She blinked back any tears, she was sick of crying. Her other foot caught up with her first one, now barely in the nursery.

And Agatha–

What made a child loved?

She couldn’t do it, not yet. She whipped back around, moving into the hall like a coward. The door was still open, maybe she didn’t have to close it. Agatha could accept it as part of the house again. She could view without engaging and, eventually, she’d be able to go and stay in the room. Yeah. Yeah, that’d work. That’s something. It’s not nothing.

No.

It was pathetic.

This is what she made of her daughter’s memory? A dusty mausoleum. A creepy shrine of the life Alex was supposed to live. Fuck, her daughter would be so ashamed. The daughter still alive was ashamed, ashamed of Agatha. She slumped against the wall, her brain forging too many atrocities at once. The thoughts produced and faded too quickly for her to discern.

What made a child loved?

“Telling me to try when all you’ve done is give up.”

No, no, she was doing better.

She was at peace.

“Then I concede."

“You are being so fucking dramatic.”

The day had been so good.

“I think I’m fucking everything up, and I- I don’t know why.”

“Mi amor, Alex didn’t make it.”

Stop it.

“You pushed me away! You didn’t want me, Agatha!”

Stop it.

“Babe, there’s no bassinet, there’s no baby crying. It was just a dream, go back to sleep.”

What made a child loved?

Fuck.

Agatha pushed herself off the wall, hyperventilating.

She was alone.

She couldn’t be alone.

Agatha ran downstairs, grabbing her keys and leaving the house before her mind had caught up to her body’s actions. The roads weren’t great, but she’d survive, after all, she always did. Nobody had to worry for Agatha because nobody as stubborn as her could hurt. Nobody as fucking difficult as her could drown inside thier own head. Nobody who ended her marriage and punished her family for her own faults could be as weak as Agatha felt in the current moment.

“I-” Agatha began, ceasing when a stranger stood before her.

“Yeah?” A blond woman, at least a decade younger than Agatha, greeted. Her beauty should’ve been the first thing that struck Agatha, but that’s not what knocked the fight out of her.

What did?

Mrs. Vidal’s AP Lit Class of ‘13 scrawled across the woman’s ample chest, Rio’s sweats on her legs. Her mouth opened, nothing came out.

“Can I help you?” The woman with a thick eastern European accent prompted. The 29? 30? Year old tilted her head, giving Agatha a real glance. “Have we met?”

Yes, that’s right, they had.

Over the phone when Rio was sick.

She worked with Rio, Agatha had seen her when she picked them up.

Oh.

Her ex had been seeing other women, and went as far as to see one right after she and Rio had–

It didn't matter what they had done together.

Clearly it didn't matter to Rio.

They were fucking their colleague.

Or going by this woman's age, they were fucking their subordinate.

Why did Agatha never feel like enough?

“Wrong unit.” She croaked, stuffing her keys in her pocket to hide the evidence. “Sorry, have a good night.”

“You too.” The younger woman smiled, softly shut the door, leaving Agatha–

Alone.

Agatha pulled on her sleeve, using it to cover her mouth as a cry clawed its way from her vocal cords, her free one clutching her stomach in an attempt to regulate her breathing. Her feet carried her back down the hall, collapsing into the elevator. She jammed her thumb against the Lobby button, doors shutting.

She steadied herself using the bar mounted to the wall as the engine whirled, vision hazy from the fluorescent lighting and tears. She’d dug herself into a cave, believing it’d protect her. Confusing the reality of the situation with her own fucking delusions.

What made her so hard to love?

What made her so easy to dismiss?

And how–

How was it all her fault?

What made a child loved?

Was she just too cold?

A baron wasteland.

Uninhabitable.

Something wrong and twisted at her core.

Stiff to the touch.

Her very being, hardened and stone.

Evil.

The doors opened, sending her tumbling out the front door. Agatha stood trembling in front of the building, the sky blackened and lifeless. Her nerves numbed to the bite of the winter weather.

What made a child loved?

Nothing Agatha ever fucking did.

The siege had lifted, Agatha surrendering.

Succumbing to what remained true–

That a burden, no matter how compliant or apologetic, will always be just that.

A burden.

Rio’s wife gulped, a thin and weak curl of her lips following. “Yeah, could be fun.”

“Mami, look!” Nicky shoved the poster in their face, too excited to notice the disdain in their demeanor. “I’m gonna frame it.”

“That’s really cool, mija.” Rio politely spoke before glancing at the reason they were even here. “Agatha, can I talk to you in the kitchen?”

Agatha tensed. “About what?”

“Dr. Vostokoff emailed me something about the insurance payment not going through.” Bullshit, an utter lie, but a necessary excuse. “Should figure it out before Nicky’s next session.”

“Fine.” Agatha muttered, giving Nicky’s shoulder a squeeze before sauntering off.

Rio let the three of them talk amongst themselves, striding into the kitchen. “What the ever living fuck?” They whisper-shouted. “I thought you were ending things?!”

Agatha whipped around, clearly pissed. “Oh? Why would I do that?!”

“Uh, gee, I don’t know…because of this weekend?” Rio threw their arms up, keeping their voice quiet for their daughter’s sake.

She scoffed. “I didn’t realize that meant anything to you.”

“Why the hell wouldn’t it?”

“You tell me.”

Rio pinched the bridge of their nose in frustration, calming down before proceeding. “Did something happen?”

“Nope.” Agatha crossed her arms, nonchalant in her response.

“Okay, baby-”

“Don’t call me that.” Agatha raised an accusatory finger. “You lost that privilege.”

“Why?” They took a step towards her, pleading. “What the fuck did I do?”

“Guess.” She hissed. “What did you do?”

“You fucking tell me! I was under the impression we were getting somewhere!”

“Yeah, me too! And I was so fucking stupid to believe otherwise!” Agatha’s voice thundered, well, for a whisper at least. “Tell me, were you just placating me?”

“Where is this coming from?! Talk to me, use your fucking words!”

“Okay,” Agatha defiantly grinned. “Here’s some words. Fuck you! This weekend was a mistake and no amount of sex can fix what's broken. I trusted you and you screwed me over.”

Rio twisted their lips, taking the verbal jab. “I didn’t screw you over, you can trust me, Agatha. I’d never…” They swallowed the hurt, they always did. “What did I do? Just tell me and I can fix it.”

“Why don’t you ask one of your girlfriends.” She spat, eyes welling.

“Jesus fucking christ! There’s no women, Agatha! There never was! I said that to make you jealous!”

“God! Is this fun for you? Do you get off on it? The lies?”

“No, you’re actually breaking my fucking heart. Again, I might add!”

“Always the fucking victim.” Agatha bunched her fists, bringing them to her head like she was about to rip out her hair. “You broke mine! You took advantage of my vulnerability, I should’ve known better.”

“I didn’t take advantage…” Rio stumbled back, because they hadn’t right?

“I was tipsy and sad and you played that god forsaken song…” Her voice wobbled. “It wasn’t real, any of it.”

The tears stung but they were nothing compared to Agatha’s words. “Is this about me? What I told you?”

“Don’t be so self righteous.” She said, lethal and purposeful. “You’re hardly in any position.”

Rio’s resolve had been slashed, mangled and turned to dust. “Why don’t you want me?”

“We both know if it wasn’t for Nicky, we would’ve been strangers by now.” Agatha looked away, the admission seeming to hurt her as much as it aimed to wound Rio. “We can’t keep beating what’s dead.” And then, as if the coffin wasn’t already sealed, Agatha nailed it shut. “We died with Alex, it’s futile to keep torturing each other.”

Rio’s jaw dropped. “That’s not true.”

“We weren’t fate, we weren’t something written in the stars. It was just chance, and we should stop pretending otherwise.”

“We can work this out in therapy-”

“I’m done with that,” Agatha sniffled, tears dribbling down her face. “I’ll do family sessions with teddy, but I don’t see a reason to continue with ours.”

“Mi amor,” Rio damn near begged, “Please, don’t push me away again.”

She shrugged, arms holding herself. “I can't live like this, Nicky deserves more."

“Nicky deserves her parents back!”

“Well, you ruined that, didn’t you?”

Rio sucked in a breath, blinking back the tears. “You know, I take a lot. I swallow and swallow,” They deflated, shaking their head. “But sometimes you just cut too fucking deep, Agatha.”

“You say that like it’s shocking.” She somberly chuckled, biting in her delivery. “You knew who you married, you knew who you divorced, you knew who you fucked on Saturday night. Right?”

“What happened in the last twelve hours to make you think that- that I’m some fucking monster?”

“Came to my senses.”

Rio’s heart beat, but it was out of time, the organ made of glass in Agatha’s hand.

“I really thought this time was different.”

“Me too.”

“You said you loved me.”

“That was before I knew better.”

Dropped carelessly onto the floor, fracturing into too many pieces to count.

Their stomach twisted, their insides gnawing. “And Alex’s anniversary?”

“You and Nicky can go, I’m sitting this year out.” Their ex said, wiping her face.

Oh.

So, Lilia had every cause for concern, because Agatha never missed visiting Alex’s grave. Even if Rio didn’t attend, they knew from their daughter that Agatha held that day as something sacred. But, Rio didn’t know how to help. They couldn’t heal her with their love, they couldn’t fix what was wrong, they couldn’t save any of it.

The salvageable parts of their marriage, the scraps of their family, all crushed into a fine powder and swept up and blown away, winding through the air as something Rio couldn’t help.

“We’re not going without you.” Rio murmured, even if Agatha didn’t want them, they were still a family, right?

“Rio, leave it alone.” Agatha stood straight and rigid. “Just…leave me alone.”

Can you really fight for someone who’s telling you to give up? Do you throw down your sword and accept what’s right in front of you? They didn’t even understand what they had done wrong, yet they were taking the loss just the same.

They didn't have a response, couldn’t formulate one. Rio turned on their heel, a booming “Mija, it’s time to go.” tumbling out of their mouth. Nicky confusedly rolled the poster, shouting her goodbyes to Agatha. Sure, dick move not to have Nicky say a proper goodbye but Rio couldn’t deal. So they collected their daughter and went home, Lilia had driven separately anyway. Obviously Agatha needed her mom more than the piss poor comfort Rio could provide. Hell, maybe Wanda could soothe Agatha better than Rio ever fucking could.

Yes, there was a petty little voice in the back of their mind, one saying tell Wanda about how you had her fiancée sobbing in bed this weekend, tell her to check Agatha’s chest and hips, tell her exactly how many times Agatha came and what she said during each and every orgasm., but that wouldn’t get them anywhere. Rio could be the secret, Rio could be the warm body only useful for a night. Because the alternative? That they were less, that they were nothing in Agatha’s eyes.

“Were you guys fighting?” Their daughter asked in the passenger's seat on the way home. “In the kitchen?”

“It was nothing.” They lied, keeping their focus on the road.

“Is it about the gift? Because, I swear, I don’t suddenly like Wanda now. If it makes you mad, I can give the poster back.”

Rio’s chest ached for their daughter. “No mi vida, it’s yours. We’re gonna frame it and I’ll hang it wherever you want.”

“So, what was the fight about?”

“Nicky, can we please just drop it? It’s not even noon and it’s been a day.”

“I hate when you guys do that. Treat me like a kid.”

“You are a kid.”

“But I’m not dumb.” She mumbled, fidgeting with the rubberband binding the poster. “You guys aren’t as sneaky as you think you are.”

What the fuck did that mean?

“Sneaky about what?”

“Nothing.” She swallowed.

Nicky swallowed.

“Your child reflects your behavior.”

Rio pulled into the loft’s parking garage, killing the engine and turning to face their daughter. “You’re right.” They nervously tapped their fingers against the steering wheel, anxiety flooding their veins. “You’re not dumb, and I should be honest with you.”

Nicky turned her body too, eyebrows shooting up her forehead. “Seriously?”

“Seriously.” Rio said, eyes darting between the console and Nicky. “There’s something I haven’t been telling you, and I should. You deserve to know, and I want to share that with you.”

“Mami…” She prompted. “I can handle it.”

“Mija,” How do you come out to your daughter? Shit, they should’ve Googled this beforehand. “There’s something… about me. Not bad. But different than what you’re used to.” Better to bite the bullet now. “I’ve never really felt super connected to womanhood, like, the binary of it.”

“Yeah…” Nicky nodded, waiting.

“And I’m certainly not connected to manhood or men, but…” They paused, because were they even making any fucking sense? “I should actually go back, how much do you know about gender vs. sex?”

“Oh my god!” Nicky snorted the same way Agatha does. “Mami, just say you’re nonbinary, you don’t have to be so awkward about it.”

Rio reeled back, eyes bugging. “What?!”

“Yeah, I already knew.” She shrugged, putting on a faux parental voice. “But I’m really glad you felt safe enough telling me, sweetie.”

“You-” They tripped over their own tongue. “You knew?”

“You hid the tape behind the communal tampons in a communal bathroom,” She flourished out her hands in an obviously type of motion. “Plus, you kept taking forever to get ready in the mornings all of a sudden. You brush your hair, teeth, and get dressed. You’re ready in, like, fifteen minutes. Then you started taking longer than me, which is saying something because I got mom’s time management skills.”

“And- and you’re fine with it?”

“I have trans friends, mami.” Nicky said, “Told you I’m not dumb.”

“Damn, your generation starts young these days…”

“Do you still want me to use ‘mami’ or is that dysphoric?" She cautiously asked. “Because it’ll take me a sec, but-”

“No, no baby.” Rio smiled, so fucking proud of the kid they had raised. “I’m always your mami, no matter what.”

“Cool.” She smiled back, face then crinkling. “Wait, is that what you guys were fighting about?”

“No, your mom knows and was fine with it.” They think, at least.

“Mom knows?!”

“Therapy this weekend.” Rio waved her off, because there was no way in hell Rio was going to tell her the truth.

“Are you going to tell me what you were arguing about, then?”

“I’m not even sure what we were fighting about, myself.”

Rio’s phone buzzed, a frantic text from Yelena saying she forgot her ID badge at Rio’s and needed to stop by and grab it. They texted her back, looking up at their daughter. “We should go up, my friend is stopping by.”

Nicky side eyed that, but got out of the car.

Once they were back in the loft, and settling back into normalcy, Yelena barged in. No knock, okay then.

“My shift starts in thirty minutes!” Yelena declared, slightly out of breath.

“It’s upstairs on my dresser.” Rio directed, leaning against the island and putting in a grocery order on their phone.

The resident took off, passing Nicky and giving a quick “Oh, hi. Nice to meet you, I’ve heard a lot about you! You have beautiful eyes!”

Nicky watched as Yelena bolted upstairs, then glared at Rio. “Please don’t tell me I have two step moms to hate.”

Rio cackled, quite loudly. “She’s a coworker, mija…And sixteen years younger than me, and not my type.”

Yelena returned, badge in hand. “Okay hurtful.” She clipped it onto her scrub top under her jacket. “Also, is that Agatha in the photo in your room?”

“Yes.” Nicky answered, scowling at Yelena. “Isn’t my mom so pretty?”

“She is.” The resident agreed. “Like a Greek goddess.” She walked over to Rio, lowly speaking so Nicky wouldn’t hear. “That is the woman who was at the door last night. I only saw her in passing when she picked you up when you were sick, but I knew she looked familiar.”

The phone simply slipped from Rio’s grip, the dots rapidly connecting. Yelena answered the door, in Rio’s clothes, at night, right after they had–

And the call with Lilia.

Oh fuck.

Chapter Notes

okay, as a preface--
TW FOR: child loss & grief, mentions of self harm (self neglect, restrictive eating, VERY VAGUE suicidal ideation) nothing is overly graphic but please take care of yourself first🖤

on another note: This chapter is very emotionally dense but so so healing at the same time, I truly love this chapter with my whole heart

enjoy!

August, 2019.

Agatha sat on the horrible metal bench, cooking away in the summer sun, surrounded by rowdy parents. She was pregnant, just barely, but it definitely didn’t make the day any more pleasant. She watched over the rim over her sunglasses as the game played out, Nicky sprinting up and down the field. Did she understand soccer? No. Was her daughter the very best at it? She might be biased, but absofuckinglutely.

“Why did I come to this?” Jen groaned next to her, fanning herself.

“Because aunts go to boring shit for the sake of the kid.” Agatha responded, pressing her water bottle to her overheated skin.

“How much longer will they be?”

“Who fucking knows, I can’t keep track. I just smile whenever teddy looks over here.”

“Rio’s lucky she gets to miss this.” Jen grumbled, obligatorily cheering when Nicky’s team had scored a goal.

Because Rio missed a lot, and often. Agatha didn’t hold it against her wife, she was aware of Rio’s insane work schedule when they had met. She didn’t appreciate her wife being gone sixty hours or more a week, but Rio made up for it. When Rio was home, she was home, entirely present and devoted to their family. She cooked and took care of their daughter, helped with the chores, doted on Agatha. So, if Rio missed some stuff, it was something Agatha would live with, because she knew her wife loved her job.

Agatha watched Nicky take off across the grass as she sarcastically joked “Wow, you're such a committed god mother.”

“I’m here, aren’t I?” Her best friend grinned, looking back to the field. “Oh!”

She jumped up onto her feet as Nicky tumbled down, hitting the dirt with a soft thud. Jen chuckled next to her, hiding it behind her hand. Agatha glared at her, lightly smacking her shoulder. “Jen!”

“I’m sorry,” Jen cackled, “Kids falling down is always funny.”

Her daughter got up, tears in her eyes as her lower lip trembled. Nicky’s coach checked on her, sending her Agatha’s way with a nod. Nicky ran over, knee bloodied and scraped, little face covered in tears.

“Mamaaaaa!” Her six-year old whined, tiny body colliding with Agatha’s.

She embraced her daughter, placing a gentle kiss on her sweaty forehead and pushing back the baby hairs that stuck out of her braids. “It’s okay, sweetheart.”

“I h-hurt my knee.” Nicky sobbed, hiccupping out her words. “I suck!”

Agatha sat back down, letting Nicky climb onto her lap. “No, you don’t. You are doing so great out there.” She smiled, wrapping an arm around her. “You don’t have to be perfect, baby. You are so brave and strong all on your own, okay? You just try your best.”

Nicky sniffled, nodding.

“Now,” She looked over to Jen. “Should we have aunt Jen patch you up?”

Jen inspected the scrape, tutting. “I think we’re going to have to amputate the whole thing, you don’t need this leg, right?”

Her daughter let out a giggle, resting her head on Agatha’s shoulder.

“I have some band aids in my bag.” Agatha tilted her head to her purse on the ground. “I guess we’ll save your leg, but just this once.”

Jen rifled through her bag, brows furrowed. “God, Agatha. How much shit do you need?” She moved fistfuls of junk around. “I mean, there’s a small drug store in here!”

“Hey, you try being a mom.” She huffed, resting her cheek against the top of her daughter’s head. “I’m carrying shit for three at this point.”

After embryo number five hadn’t stuck, they immediately did another round with number six, their final one. Which was a miracle, especially since the fertility drugs they used this time around had severely fucked up her cycle. Her first scan was in a week, her and Rio going back and forth about names already. She had announced the pregnancy to her wife by dressing Nicky in a Snoopy and Woodstock Big Sister to Be, March 2020 shirt. Stupid and tacky, but Rio’s joy and shock had been worth it.

Jen finally found a bandage, some tissues, and the Neosporin. She used some of Agatha’s water to rinse off Nicky’s knee, dabbing it with the tissues, applying the gel, and sticking on the band aid. “Well, Miss Vidal,” Jen said, pretending she was delivering news to a patient. “I believe you’ll make a full recovery.”

Agatha gasped, peering down at Nicky. “See how brave you are?! You are so good, hon. A champ, really.”

Her daughter laughed, the tears vanishing and being replaced with a big smile. “Thank you, aunt Jen.”

Jen threw all the excess into Agatha’s bag. “All in a day’s work, and you can thank me by getting back out there.”

“What do you say?” She helped Nicky jump down, rubbing her back. “Think you can go out there and kick some ass?”

“Can we get ice cream after?” Nicky asked, puppydog eyes on full display.

“I respect the hustle, so yes.” Agatha snorted. “Now, go!”

Her daughter bolted back to her coach, sprinting onto the field a minute later, fully rehabilitated.

“I should charge you for that exquisite healthcare.” Jen muttered.

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I’ll buy you a cone.”

The way sugar dissolves into tea, the way honey melts on your tongue. That’s how she wished she could go, seamlessly and quietly, no fuss. Her body weightless under the surface, the world muted as the water lapped. The bath had cooled, but Agatha kept her head under, lungs beginning to burn, begging for air. Her heart slowed, limbs floating. But, she stayed down. If she never resurfaced, then nothing existed. She could ignore the day, ignore Rio and Wanda.

No body, no pain.

“Agatha.” A muffled voice echoed.

Her eyes snapped open, a blurred image of Wanda standing over the tub. Jesus fucking christ, what now? Agatha sat up, reflexively gasping for air, curling her knees to her chest. Any marks on her body had healed, so there was no need to hide, it was just instinctive. “Yeah?”

Wanda seemed confused, but didn’t address the behavior. “Is this it for your half of the guest list?” She held up the scrap of notebook paper Agatha had given her this morning.

“Sure is.” Agatha smiled on que, masking her inner turmoil. “Why do you ask?”

“There’s, like, ten names on here and two are Nicky and Lilia.”

“I don’t see the issue.”

She sat on the edge of the tub, frowning. “Babe, there’s got to be more people.” Wanda brought a hand up to cradle Agatha’s cheek. “What about your mom?”

“Lilia’s on there-”

“No, I mean your real mom.”

Agatha bitterly chuckled, gently removing Wanda’s grasp on her face. “I didn’t realize I had a fake mom.”

“Not like that,” Wanda sighed, patience already worn thin. “I know you see Lilia as your mom, but you never talk about your bio parents. I figured it would be nice if you guys could reconnect before the wedding.”

“Hon, my father was a drunk who skipped town the second the strip turned blue, and Evanora is Satan. They don’t put you into foster care for shits and giggles.” Agatha had never told Wanda the full extent of her childhood and didn’t plan to, Evanora might as well be dead in her eyes, or dead for real, Agatha didn’t keep tabs on her. “Leave it alone.”

“Are you being stubborn because you’re not going to see Alex today?” Her fiancée asked casually, like one would about the weather and not Agatha’s dead child. “Because we can still go, I’m sure Rio and Nicky would love it if you were there. I can even stay in the car if it’ll be a big thing for both of them.”

“I’m not going.” Agatha said, resolute in the decision. She didn’t want to see Rio, she didn’t want to mourn Alex, she didn’t want to feel everything that today entailed.

It had been six days since she backslid with her ex, five since she found out about the busty blond, and four since breaking things off. Rio had called and texted, swearing that the woman was a coworker and that they’d never do that. Hell, they had even shown up to the house a couple days back, demanding to talk about it all. Agatha had taken their keys, ripping off the one to the townhome, and chucked the rest into the bushes, locking the front door behind her and leaving Rio in the cold. They had hung around for about an hour before giving up and leaving to presumably pick up Nicky from piano.

Even if Rio was telling the truth, it wouldn’t change what she had told them on Monday. “This weekend was a mistake and no amount of sex can fix what's broken.” She hadn’t been referring to their marriage, she’d been referring to herself. Agatha wasn’t just broken, she was living life tattered into pieces. She couldn’t get anything right, she couldn’t face Alex’s room or her grave, she couldn’t be alone.

“Did something happen while I was gone?” Wanda’s eyes bore into her soul. “It would explain why my future wife ghosted me.”

“I apologized for that.” Agatha murmured, dropping her head against the porcelain of the tub. “Are you going to keep guilting me with it?”

Wanda’s mouth formed a tight and unsettling smile. “Just, try to round up more people. The engagement party is already underway, we’ll do the family dinner this weekend-”

“I thought I vetoed that.”

“Well, I reached out to Rio and she agreed-”

“They.” Agatha corrected, the pronoun switch being blasted in the family group chat that included Lilia and excluded Wanda. She had informed her after Rio had sent the text, the switch had yet to be made on Wanda’s end.

“They agreed that a family dinner could be good if you’re not going to the gravesite today.” Wanda said, annoyed. “I’m trying, Agatha. I am trying to be a part of this family despite nobody, seemingly not even you, wanting me to!”

“So you text my ex wife?!” Agatha snapped, water swishing around. “Not the way to go about it, in my humble opinion!"

Wanda stood up, paper crumpling in her fist. “You’re so fucking difficult!”

“Sorry.” Agatha sighed, slinking back down into the tub and submerging herself once again. The other woman yelled something else that was muffled before stomping away and slamming the door behind her.

Finally, peace.

Wanda had left for work by the time Agatha got out of the bath, she’d called in sick, just like every year before. Maria already knew, already had a sub booked. She thought about going to school, distracting herself. But then she’d run the risk of weeping in front of her students, and she couldn’t ruin her street cred like that.

Agatha didn’t feed herself, didn’t take care of her hair or skin after the bath. She put on some pajama pants and that old Red Sox hoodie and fucking paced down the hall. Opening Alex’s door couldn’t hurt, she doubted she could get lower than how she felt right now. Back and forth, to the door and then the banister, back and forth. She knew she didn’t deserve to visit Alex’s grave, but what about her room?

Her fingers hovered around the knob, forehead resting against the wood of the door. She lifted her head, letting it softly fall forward again. As if she could knock some sense into herself. And she knew, she fucking knew, how pathetic it was. How miserable a person had to be to struggle with something so easy.

Just twist the knob.

Just twist the knob.

Just twist. The fucking knob.

Fuck’s sake–

“Mom!” Nicky called out, two sets of footsteps climbing the stairs.

She whipped around, distancing herself from Alex’s room. “Teddy?”

Her daughter bounded up, black pants, shirt, and peacoat on, a house key dangling from her fingers. “Told you she'd be home.”

Rio appeared a minute later, matching their daughter in the mourning attire. “You were right, mi vida.”

Her eyes flickered between the two. “What is this?”

Nicky confidently said “We’ve come to kidnap you. We’re going to see Alex, and we’re not leaving without you.”

She looked to Rio, who just nodded, face etched with sorrow. “She deserves to see her family again, all together this year.”

“I can’t.” Agatha whispered, crossing her arms. “I can’t this time, I’m sorry.”

“Is it mami?” Nicky cocked her head, pointing at Rio behind her. “Because they’re real quiet, you won’t even know they’re there.”

“No, baby. It’s not that.”

“Also,” Rio nudged their daughter. “Hey.”

Nicky walked closer, hands in her pockets. “Then what is it?”

Agatha tried to blink back the tears, tried to speak without breaking down. “It- It’s just too hard.”

Their daughter nodded, considering. “Alex would want you there. I want you there.” She pulled out those fucking puppydogs eyes. “Please.”

What kind of mother was she, to not even see her daughter on her birthday. She was sure she had given everything. Every tear, drop of blood, ounce of sweat–

And it’d never be enough.

“We can make it quick, if that would make it easier.” Rio offered, staying put at the top of the steps. “And it’s nice outside, a whopping forty degrees. Thank you, climate change.”

She pressed her lips together, her daughter reaching out a hand and grabbing Agatha’s, holding it. “I’ll help you get dressed and brush your hair," Nicky smiled, “I know you hate combing it out.”

“Let us help you, Agatha.” Her ex said, fingers tapping against the banister. “We’ll do it together.”

“Okay.” She rasped, too tired to fight.

“Okay.” Her daughter repeated, tugging Agatha towards her room. “Mami, give us thirty minutes!”

Rio took a seat on the top step. “An hour, got it.”

She sat in front of the mirror in the ensuite bathroom as her thirteen year old carefully detangled her hair, being the fucking adult in the situation. Agatha stared at her hands in her lap, stray tears dripping onto her palms. Nicky didn’t point it out, just moved the comb through her locks.

“I’m sorry.” Agatha croaked. “You shouldn’t have to do this.”

Her daughter didn't falter, softly undoing another knot. “I don’t mind.”

“Why?” Agatha looked up at her daughter through the mirror, eyes bloodshot and cheeks sunken in.

Nicky shrugged, smoothing out the strands. “Because you always told me I don’t have to be perfect, and it made me feel better.” She set down the comb, brown doe eyes locking onto Agatha’s through the reflection. “You don’t have to be perfect, mom.”

“You’re being nice to me and it’s throwing me off.”

Nicky rounded her, perching on the counter. “I’m sorry. If mami coming out has taught me anything, it’s that I want you guys to be happy. Both of you.” Her eyes went glassy. “I know I’ve made things rough for you, and maybe it’s ‘cause I thought mami needed me more after the divorce. You moved on first and it hurt.” Her voice shook, but she didn’t let it stop her. “I was angry. I still am. Because my sister is gone, and losing her made me lose you too. After a while, I got it in my head that you and mami broke up because I wasn’t enough to keep you guys together.”

Agatha placed her hand on Nicky’s knee, trying to comfort when her own cup was already barren and empty. “I am so sorry, sweetheart. I promise, it was never you.” She grinned, reaching up and gently tucking a lock of Nicky’s hair behind her ear. “You are my everything, and more than enough. I wouldn’t trade you for the world.”

“Can I say something, like, not as a smartass remark or snide comment?”

“Of course.”

“I wish you liked yourself the way you love me.”

Oh.

Nicky sniffled, jumping off the counter and rummaging through the drawers. “Is the blowdryer in the other bathroom?”

“The one off the den.” Agatha answered, her daughter’s words stinging worse than antiseptic in a fresh wound.

Just as bloody, just as brutal.

The three of them climbed into Rio’s car, Agatha in the passenger’s seat and Nicky in the back, similar to old times. Her ex parked in the lot of the cemetery, hopping out first to open her door for her. Rio’s hand stretched out, an offering, a truce perhaps. Agatha took it, her legs feeling like a newborn foal's as her loafer hit the pavement.

The day was nice, all things considered. It was sunny and pretty warm for February in Boston, the grass saturated in melted ice and snow, muddy as the three of them wound through the sprawling plot of land. Nobody spoke as they walked, Nicky carrying the bouquet, clearly handmade by her ex wife. Agatha hesitated at the fork in the pathway, knowing Alex’s grave was maybe only twenty feet beyond it.

Rio stopped, noticing Agatha’s halting in less than a second. Their eyes already shone with tears, a thick “She’s waiting, mi amor.” hitting Agatha eardrums. Nicky approached her, shifting the bouquet to her other hand and using her free one to grab Agatha’s. “We got you.” Nicky said, fingers intertwined. She felt her throat close, but took another step, snagging her ex’s hand as she did so. Even if she and Rio weren’t on the best of terms, that got pushed aside for now.

For Alex.

The three of them walked side by side, hand in hand, until they reached Alex’s headstone. They stood in a line in front of the grave, pristine in its upkeep, seedlings beginning to bloom as spring approached. The grounds crew here always kept Alex’s grave immaculate, which they should for how much it cost. The stone was marbled charcoal, a small Snoopy and Woodstock engraved in the top right corner, Agatha had paid extra for it.

Alexandria Emmet Vidal

February 20th, 2020

Your Mothers Love You So

Agatha visited at least a few times a year, but her daughter’s birthday always made it hit harder, stealing all the air from her lungs. Nicky let go of her hand, pulling out a violet, Alex’s birth flower, from the bunch before passing it to Agatha. Rio did the same, letting go of her and plucking out a flower. Agatha stood between them, limp in her grasp on the bundle of carefully manicured flowers Rio had grown and picked, especially for their daughter on her birthday.

Nicky let out a breath, looking at her parents. “Guess I’ll start?”

“If you want to, otherwise-” Agatha offered, her words already wet.

“I can do it.” Nicky said, cautiously kneeling down in front of the headstone. “Hey, Alex.” She delicately placed the flower atop the marble. “Been a minute, sorry. It’s just been cold as shit and you live outside.” Agatha let out a small snort, Rio chuckling beside her. “We miss you like crazy, but I hope you’re at peace. Maybe one day, we’ll catch up. I know you would’ve been a great little sister, even if you did steal my stuff, you would’ve come in handy as a scapegoat.” Their daughter used the sleeve of her jacket to dry her eyes. “I love you, and wish we’d had more time with you. You’re always with us, forever.” Nicky hastily got up, taking her place next to Agatha again. “Okay, someone else, go.”

Agatha wound her arm around Nicky’s shoulders, placing a chaste kiss on her temple. “You did great, hon.”

Rio cleared their throat, steeling themself. Their steps towards her grave were unsure, but they knelt down without a thought, another flower laid against the stone. “Hi, mija.” They tilted their head, hands clasped in their lap. “I’ve got some birth-” They hiccupped back a sob. “Some birthdays to catch up on, and I’m so sorry I’ve missed them. But, there’s not a day that goes by where I don’t think about you.” The breeze whistled through the trees, the leaves minimal due to the season. “I know you would’ve been just as whip smart as your mom, as empathetic as your sister. You would’ve been kind, and so fucking cool.” They tucked their tongue against their cheek, the tears trailing onto their lips. “I wanna believe you felt every ounce of love we poured into you. I wanna believe you felt me hold you. I- I hope I was able to provide you that comfort, because you didn’t deserve to go. We might’ve missed each other, but I loved you, I do love you, all the same. And, mi cielo, I’m…I’m so- so-” Rio’s voice shattered, shoulders hunching as the cries kept coming. “Sorry. I’m sorry I wasn’t there in time, I’m sorry I made the call that- that-”

Agatha’s heart needled, taking mercy on Rio and placing her hand on their shoulder as she knelt down next to her ex. The earth was soft beneath her knees, the mud staining her pants. She placed the bouquet in front of the grave, leaning it against the stone. She blew out a deep breath, Rio grabbing her hand and clutching it as though it were the only tether they had left to reality. They didn’t look at her though, gaze remaining on Alex’s grave.

She gnawed at her lower lip, the guilt and the grief swirling in her head. “Hi, my baby.” Agatha felt Nicky sidle up beside her, fingers lacing with Agatha’s once again. “Took us a while but we’re here.” All four of them in one place at one time since the funeral, where Nicky had bawled out of confusion, and Agatha couldn't do anything but the same. Back then, Rio simply watched as the infant-sized casket was lowered, not a tear shed or an emotion displayed. “I, um, I wasn't going to see you, didn't feel like it’d be something that you would want.” The tsunami of tears and snot overtook her, weeping as she fought to speak. “Sometimes, it’s too hard to face you. I worry every day. If I did enough for you, if I should’ve done more. I really, really tried for you, hon.” Rio finally looked at her, as did Nicky. “I know it doesn’t mean much now, but…”

“It still means a lot, mom.”

Agatha’s lip beaded with blood as her teeth worked, quickly swiping her tongue as she stared at the stone that represented her daughter. “I dream about your cries. I fantasize about your laughs, what they’d sound like. I- I wish for your peace, wherever you are. I love you. Soooo much.” She bowed her head in defeat, because there was nothing she could say that would be adequate enough. No scrambling of words would amount to her child, to Alex. She sighed, “Hera better be taking good care of you, I’ll kick her ass if she’s not.”

The sun beamed down, reflecting off the marble, shining onto them as they lapsed into silence. She didn’t let go of Rio or Nicky, sandwiched in the middle as gentle sobs and tender breaths were released. Perhaps this, just this, was something to Alex. Hopefully it brought her some solace, to know her family, however bruised, could heal long enough for her.

She didn’t keep track of how long they sat there, rooted just as the seedlings. Nicky got up first, excusing herself back to the car, blubbering and needing a minute. It was so quiet when Rio finally spoke again. “Thank you…for coming with us.”

“Thanks for kidnapping me.” She whispered, hand warm in her ex wife’s.

They ran their thumb along her own, peering over at her. “I think you’re right.”

“I usually am.” Agatha sadly smiled. “About what?”

“Sex won’t fix us. I didn’t sleep with Yelena, I haven’t slept with any woman other than you in eighteen years. Haven't deigned to even touch someone who wasn't you, haven't felt the urge to.” Rio’s face crinkled, not in pain, but acceptance. “I can’t bring Alex back, and I can’t mend what hurts you. I want to, I've tried to, but you have to do that yourself. I love you. I always will, I’ve never stopped.” Her ex squeezed her hand. “But you don’t need a wife right now, you need support. You need people in your corner regardless of expectations. So, that’s what I’ll be, for the meantime. ‘Cause you’re not on your own, and I’m not bailing this time around.” Rio chastely kissed Agatha’s knuckles, so fast that she would’ve missed it had time not been moving in slow motion, the warmth gone before it even registered. “You don’t have to be with me, but please, don’t marry her.”

Agatha opened her mouth, devoid of a response as she watched honeyed eyes plead. Rio got up, brushing the grass off their legs. “You deserve someone who’d fight for you. You deserve good things, Agatha. We both do.” They made sure the flowers were secure against the headstone. “We’ll wait for you in the car, take all the time you need.”

As they began to walk away, they called out “You were wrong about everything else, though.”

She watched their silhouette fade away, becoming smaller and smaller until Rio disappeared altogether. Agatha whipped her head to look at Alex. “Please tell me you heard that.” She uttered in disbelief, speaking as if Alex would agree. “I fucking know, right?”

Agatha brushed her hand along the carvings, making sure it was clear of dirt or debris, like a mother cleaning off their child’s face. “Happy birthday, baby. I’d do it all over again for you.” She pushed herself up, twirling the engagement ring around her finger as she gingerly walked the winding road yet again. The end bringing her family, her daughter and wife. Agatha paused just before the cemetery gates, rolling her head back, letting the warmth of the sun bathe her, face tilted up to the sky. The wind was cold, brisk. A butterfly passing by, just a hair shy of her nose. Her eyes focused on it as it kept going on its way, floating farther into the surrounding trees. Its wings blue, flecks of purple detailed throughout, almost pearlescent.

Odd for winter, no?

She stumbled past the gates, getting into the passengers side. “Did you guys see that butterfly?”

“Mhh?” Nicky hummed from the back.

Rio’s eyes scanned around. “No, what’d it look like?”

“Blue and purple, kind of silvery.”

“Glaucopsyche Iygdamus.” Rio said, because of course they knew that. “Also referred to as Silvery Blues, ironically enough. The weather must finally be nice enough for them.”

Or, it was more.

A sign.

Fate.

Agatha let it go, putting on her seatbelt. Her daughter poked her head out, eyes puffy. “Not to ruin the whole tone of the day, but can we get food?”

The morning had blurred into the afternoon, so whatever Poptart Nicky had scarfed down for breakfast probably wasn’t cutting it anymore. Rio nodded, looking at Agatha. “Have you eaten today? You hungry?”

Agatha hadn’t eaten since Wednesday, but instead of admitting that, she said “Yeah, I could eat.”

“Ohhh, we could get some burgers from Theo’s.” Her daughter threw out. “We haven’t all gone in forever.”

“I don’t know if I can take the public today, teddy.” Even if it was a hole-in-the-wall mom and pop burger joint, Agatha didn’t want to deal with people who weren’t already in this car.

“We’ll do a pick up order.” Rio was already on their phone. “You want your usual, no onion?”

Her usual had not been usual in years, but, “Please.”

They picked up the food, driving back to the townhouse to eat. They sat at the dinner table, takeout boxes sprawled on top. Agatha actually began eating her burger, noticing Rio grimacing at their own. “What’s wrong?”

Rio shook their head. “Nothing, they just put tomatoes on it.”

And that meant that the whole thing was contaminated in Rio’s mind.

Agatha snickered, pushing hers, free of tomatoes, towards them and taking theirs, switching the burgers. “Fixed it.”

“But that has onion.”

She took off the top bun, plucking off the onions and putting all of them onto the burger that was now Rio’s. “There.”

“Thanks.” Her ex chirped, tucking into their meal.

Nicky happily ate her lunch, seemingly content. “We should do this every year.”

“Yeah?” Agatha said through a bite of her burger. “Fun day?”

“No.” Her daughter raised her brows, lips quirked. “But, it was nice to be together without fighting. Alex would be proud of us.”

“I agree.” Rio spoke, mouth muffled with food. “I’m proud of us too.”

Agatha set her burger down, her voice slightly hoarse from crying. “Thanks for getting me. This is…” Her heart swelled, feeling somewhat renewed. “I needed it.” She wasn’t aware just how much, but it made the day easier to digest.

“I told mami as much.” Nicky rolled her eyes.

She looked to Rio. “It wasn’t your idea to bring me along?”

They nodded towards their daughter. “All teddy. Only reason I agreed to family dinner with Mr. Blobby is 'cause I thought you wouldn't come with us.”

Agatha’s view snapped onto Nicky across from her. “Really?”

Nicky had half a fry dangling out of her mouth as she responded “You’re trying your best, you just needed a push...or a hard shove.”

The care Nicky had shown today, all bestowed independently, out of nothing more than her daughter not wanting Agatha to feel alone. For all Agatha’s faults, for all of hers and Rio’s together, they got Nicky right. “How the fuck are you so great?”

“Unexplained medical mystery.” Her daughter smirked. “‘Cause you two are too lame for it to be genetics.”

“Uh!” Rio gawked, slightly offended. “I’m very cool.”

“You knew the scientific name for a butterfly.” Nicky deadpanned, then pointing to Agatha. “And you spent hours researching tape and sending me links to cross reference the reviews.”

Her ex’s stare flew over to her. “Tape?”

Agatha sighed dismissively. “There’s a few packages on the way to the loft. Various brands with different adhesives to see what works, don’t try any of them until the blistering you told me about clears up.” She poignantly explained, evading eye contact. It wasn’t out of something deeper, it would just bother her until she ensured the issue was solved. Especially because she knew Rio wouldn’t scour all the reddit threads and other bullshit for feedback on what was considered the best. No, it was just reasonable for her to fix the one fucking thing she could. That was all.

“Nerds.” Nicky murmured, finishing her food and standing to discard the takeout box. “Does anyone want anything while I’m up? I need something to drink.”

“You can say that again.” She winked. “Is it a reasonable time to open wine?”

Rio checked their watch. “3PM.”

“I’ll take it.” Agatha groaned, getting up. “You in?”

“I gotta drive us back to the loft.”

Oh, that’s right.

Out of a pure leap of faith, Agatha casually mentioned “You guys could always stay here tonight.”

“Where would I sleep?”

“You can bunk with teddy.”

Nicky walked off, shouting “It’s times like these I wish we had a guest room.”

Rio leaned back in the chair, weary in their questioning. “How would Wanda feel about that?”

“Wanda isn’t on the deed, and I can tell her to stay at her place tonight.”

“And what about all the other nights?”

“Rio,” She lowly warned. “One thing at a time.”

“Fine, do you have red?”

“Merlot.”

They frowned. “Eugh, okay.”

She texted Wanda, silencing her phone afterwards, and poured two glasses of wine. Agatha met up with Nicky and Rio in the living room, flipping channels and finding a rerun marathon of old Grey’s Anatomy episodes, which Rio loathed due to the medical inaccuracies but Nicky loved. Not super age appropriate, but she had bigger things to worry about, frankly.

Nicky sat in between them, blanket splayed over their laps as the sun set. The living room was dim as episode after episode played, Agatha stomaching the operating scenes. They weren’t traumatic by any means, just slightly nauseating. Upon the millionth scene where two characters hooked up, their daughter piped up. “How did you guys meet? You never told me.”

They absolutely had, but it was when she was too young to remember, probably a very watered down version of the real story. Agatha grinned, her daughter tucked against her side. “At a bar called Emmet’s. I went in for a drink after a break up, then I saw your mami.”

“I can’t imagine you guys young.”

“Oh, we had whole lives before you, mi vida.” Rio laughed, arm slung on the back of the couch. “Your mom was relentless.”

“God forbid a woman know what she wants.” Agatha pursed her lips. “Picture your mami, but with fewer tattoos, in a muscle tank and ripped up jeans. They were sitting at the bar and I very respectfully asked to join them.”

“Nothing compared to those low-rise jeans and baby tee you had on, and you commandeered the stool next to mine! Basically staked your claim!”

“I don’t recall that.” She haughtily raised her chin. “I sat down, we flirted, and…” Well, she couldn’t say that Rio had fucked her in the bathroom so damn excellently she thought she’d seen the light. “A few weeks later, we ran into each other again. I actually went back most nights for almost a month hoping they’d be there.”

“You did?” Rio sat up a bit in surprise. “You never told me that.”

“A hunter never tells its prey when it's destined to be dinner.” Agatha replied, absently playing with the ends of her daughter’s hair. “And they asked me out, and the rest was history.”

“Damn,” Nicky snorted, eyeing Rio. “Mom ‘masterminded’ your ass!”

“You always said it was chance! Fate!” They accused, pointing a finger.

“Yeah, I lied. Sometimes you gotta make your own fate, stack the deck.”

“Stack the deck you did.” Rio commented, slumping against the couch once more.

Nicky sniffled, quickly wiping her face. “Sorry.”

“Hon, what’s wrong? Did I say some-”

“No, no.” Her daughter curled her knees to her chest, just out of instinct. “It sounded really special.”

Her ex filled the gap, bypassing the elephant of their daughter’s parents no longer being together. “No, things got special once we had you. Which is saying something, because your mom crushed my hand so hard during labor, I thought I’d never operate again.”

“Oh, you’re fine.” Agatha breathed out, a smile playing at her lips. “Didn’t even fracture a bone.”

Nicky chuckled. “Small price to pay.”

“I’d pay much bigger for you, mija.”

And they had, in the toll of their marriage and second child.

Agatha excused herself to the kitchen, refilling her glass, Rio trailing after and typing on their phone. She pulled out the cork, wine flowing. “Work?”

“Uh, yeah. I’m just letting them know I won’t make it in tomorrow.”

A monumental gesture, because they must’ve already taken off to visit Alex today. Rio was not casual about missing work, never had been, it was always a priority.

“You don’t have to do that.”

Rio tucked their phone away in their pocket, extending their glass. “I’m here. I want to be here.”

Agatha poured them some, putting the bottle back in the fridge. “I’m sorry.” She turned around to face them. “For Monday. I was trying to hurt you and…”

“You succeeded.” Rio finished, tone holding no malice, only fact. “I appreciate the apology, but it won’t mean anything if we don’t do better.”

“I know.” Agatha sighed, grabbing her glass. “Can- can you come with me for a minute?”

“Agatha-”

“Just-” She started moving, motioning them along. Rio did so, following as she went upstairs, stopping before Alex’s door. “I- I can’t go in. I’ve been trying. I swear, I was so close…”

Rio’s gaze softened, reaching out their fingers to trace the A on the door. “Why now?”

“To do better.” She whispered. “There’s a whole room in this house that I can’t touch because I’m too pitiful to even walk in.”

“You’re not pitiful.” They immediately corrected. “I doubt I could do any better.”

“You’re already doing better.” Agatha scoffed, taking a sip so the alcohol burned more than the words. “You had your big breakthrough and now you’re cured.”

“You think I’m cured?”

“Seems like it.”

“Agatha,” Rio exhaled, “It torments me. Every kid I treat, every surgery I perform. You know, sometimes I dream about it? Alice’s voice echoing over and over again. I can’t look at a clock without something as benign as a time of day stabbing me. I can’t- I can’t see you or our daughter without a punch to the gut.”

“How do you stand it?” She asked, near silently.

Rio shrugged as if to say Whatta ya gonna do? “Because what’s the alternative?”

“What are you guys doing?” Nicky’s voice broke through, waiting at the top of the steps.

“Drinking and commiserating.” Agatha said, pointing at the door. “Discussing the benefits of renting a wrecking ball.”

Their daughter shuffled down the hall, hand shooting out and grasping the doorknob. “You want me to?”

Rio stared at Agatha.

Agatha stared at Rio.

“You don’t have to do that, baby. It could be too much for you.”

“Oh, I go in here all the time.” Nicky turned the knob. “I mean, not all the time, but it was my room at one point too. It made me feel kind of comforted, to be close to her, connected somehow. I don’t touch anything, though. I usually just sit in the rocking chair and read or sketch with my headphones on.”

“You do?” She squeaked.

“Only when you won’t notice, I know how it is for you.” Nicky pushed, letting the door swing open. “There’s nothing bad in here,” She waltzed in as though it was the simplest thing in the world. “It’s all just Alex.”

It’s all just Alex.

Nicky offered out her hand to Agatha, using the other to switch on the lights. “It’s not so scary.”

Understatement of the millennium.

She cautiously took it, letting her daughter tug her across the threshold. And though her mind was screaming, her body felt strangely content, keeping the thoughts at bay. Agatha set her wine down, reaching out to Rio. “C’mon, I’m not doing this shit alone.” Her voice rocky, tears brimming. She couldn’t do it alone, so maybe, doing it together was what she had been missing.

They set down their own glass, taking her hand and crossing through the doorframe. Rio grabbed Nicky’s free hand, standing in the room, eyes darting around like the memories were washing over them all at once.

“See?” Their daughter beamed, carrying more weight than she was aware of. “Not so scary.”

She relaxed, using the physical touch to keep herself planted. “No, it’s not.”

“Why the fuck are you so wise?” Rio muttered, shimmying their shoulder to catch a few stray tears. “You’re a pre-teen.”

“Again, medical mystery.” Nicky snarked, gleefully holding her mom’s hands. “I’m probably the smartest among us, so this actually checks out.”

And the periwinkle paint didn’t seem so dull this time, the empty crib didn’t ache from the inside out but rather pinched and twisted. The cascades of blues and purples didn’t seem so frigid, but familiar. Life had returned to the four walls, if only temporarily. Agatha smiled solemnly, her brain winning out as it told her to flee. “I think it’s time for bed, yeah?”

“Yeah.” Rio parroted, letting go of Agatha and their daughter as though they were afraid it'd start to burn like holy water does to the undeserving, the three of them filing out and turning off the lights.

A baby step, but one Agatha could say she had conquered.

And she didn’t do it alone.

They all went through their routines, Agatha loaning Rio a toothbrush and some pjs before tending to herself. It was almost midnight when she entered Nicky’s room to say goodnight, fondly looking on at Rio and their daughter under the covers. Nicky was showing them something on her phone. “So you have to guess before they make the cut.”

“That’s cake?!”

“No, mami, we don’t know yet. That's the whole point.” Nicky peeked over her screen, greeting Agatha. “You wanna see?”

“What the hell, sure.” She climbed in on the other side of her daughter, leaning over to watch the screen. “It’s cake, you can tell by the lines. That’s not stitching, it’s fondant.”

“No way,” Rio argued, engrossed at the sight. “That’s a purse, the leather looks way too real.”

Nicky giggled, hovering her thumb. “Wanna find out?”

“Play the damn video!”

“¡Ándale!”

She clicked the screen, a knife coming into view as it sliced through, or attempted to. The blade couldn’t break past the leather, revealing it to not be cake.

“Ha!” Rio shouted, “I knew it!”

“I’m not wearing my glasses!”

“Go get them,” Nicky quipped, “There’s a billion of these, we can do a rematch.”

“Fine.” Agatha bolted to her bedroom and back, glasses on her nose as she settled back into bed. “Gimme another, this is a point of pride now.”

So, they laid in bed, Nicky queuing up nonsensical video after nonsensical video. A waste of time, truly Agatha could feel herself losing brain cells. Inexplicably, it was the happiest she could remember being in a while, a soothing balm on the day. Who won more rounds is…not important. Around 1AM, they were all exhausted enough to give up, Rio barely conscious by the final video. She began to get up to go to her room, Nicky’s grasp stopping her. Her daughter drowsily curled around her, Rio on Nicky’s opposite side. “Stay.”

Agatha went slack at the plea, head cradled by the pillow as her daughter slumped onto her shoulder. She kissed the top of her head, fingers carding through her hair. “Goodnight, hon. I love you.”

Nicky wiggled in closer, Rio already dead asleep next to her. “Night, mama. I love you too.”

There was something lodged against her throat, Agatha realized. Three sets of limbs all tangled with one another, she wasn’t too sure whose hand was lightly running along her forearm. She lazily blinked, confirming that it was her daughter’s nose digging into her neck, and her ex wife’s fingers on her arm. Rio wasn’t looking at her, but their phone, the touch being mindless muscle memory. Agatha scrunched her face, Nicky's steady puffs of air hitting her skin, sound asleep.

Rio’s gaze slid over to her, lips forming a wiry grin, whispering “She still sleeps on you like she did when she was little.”

Agatha smiled, the memories of Nicky as an infant burrowing right in the crook of her neck, holding her just as tightly as she was currently. “Still a teddy bear.” She whispered back, her feet shuffling beneath the covers like a cricket’s. Her daughter always slept in a tight ball, full fetal position, knees pulled up. So, the foot she just brushed was definitely not her daughter’s.

“I took pictures.” They said, locking their phone and dropping it in the covers, not pulling their foot back. It wasn’t even skin on skin contact, they both had socks on for gods sake.

So, she kept it there, barely moving. “You didn’t.”

“I sure as hell did.”

“I spent all of yesterday crying and my hair is a rat’s nest, I probably look awful.”

“No, you in the mornings was always my favorite.” Rio replied without a second thought. “Plus, it’s good to have collateral to embarrass her with in the future.”

“Oh,” Agatha snorted, her daughter grumbling but not waking. “She’ll kill us.”

"I'd like to see her try.” Rio rasped, face illuminated by the soft glow of sun leaking in through the blinds. Their foot brushed against hers, purposefully. “How are you feeling?”

Safe.

It was sweet, all things considered, but “You don’t have to do that.”

“Do what?”

“Treat me like I’m crazy.”

“You’re not crazy, we all endured a lot yesterday. I’m checking on you.”

“Kind of sad, but in a peaceful way, if that makes sense.”

Rio stood in the kitchen, their old kitchen, whisking the batter. Yes, Agatha’s fridge was barren, cabinets empty, but they were able to get the necessities scraped together. And they were happy to do it, cook a meal for their wife and child, like old times. Yesterday had been fucking brutal, but more satisfying than they had anticipated. A way to self-flagulate, because Agatha was, above all else, a raging masochist. And though there were much healthier outlets for that, their wife needed to do the work herself. Rio had pulled the thread, given her a headstart, but only she could unweave what was tangled. Rio would wait, standby and help her up when she stumbled, but couldn’t do it for her. Which killed them a little bit, but Rio couldn’t remedy what they weren't aware of.

There was a faint buzz from the island, Rio whipping around. Agatha’s phone, face down, must’ve been left in here last night. They set down the bowl, scoping around to make sure they were alone, and innocently picked it up. They stared at the screen, Agatha and Nicky years ago, locked. Rio shouldn’t, that’s an invasion of privacy. However, their thumbs moved faster, typing in Nicky’s birthday as the passcode. Nope. Okay, Alex’s. Also no.

Rio sighed, leaning their forearms on the island, they doubted it’d work, but they punched in the digits anyway.

060207

The phone unlocked, and Rio smiled.

06/02/07, their anniversary.

Take that, Pippi Longstocking.

Rio opened the messages from Wanda, several from last night, more this morning. Looked to be a lot of Zillow listings for homes out in the burbs, none of which Agatha would like, Rio knew. They also knew that Agatha would never sell the townhouse, this was their family’s home, she’d never leave it for a cookie cutter Tim Burton satirical nightmare in a fucking cul-de-sac with an HOA. Not the type of person Agatha was, and Wanda didn’t seem to understand that. Then they scrolled all the way down to the most recent message, the one from just a minute ago.

Wanda, 9:41am: Be there in two

“Are you snooping through mama’s phone?” Nicky’s voice carried, their thirteen year old standing on the other side of the island with her arms crossed.

“¡Carajo!” Rio yelped, startled. “Scared the fuck outta me.”

Their daughter smirked, unbothered. “Anything good?”

No, it was all disturbingly not good.

They locked the phone, putting it back the same way they’d found it. “This never happened.”

Nicky smiled back, all too sweetly. “Oh ‘puta’ is just another word for ‘pretty’ in Spanish, you should try it on my mom sometime. Score some brownie points.”

“Agatha has summers off, it only makes sense to plan it for July and the honeymoon for August.” She winked, “I have some connects in the wedding industry, so a rush wedding won’t be too difficult.”

Summer?

A gesture loses its weight when it’s conditional.

Atta girl.

“I know that, I’ve made progress with her.” Wanda bitterly chuckled. “I’ve worked my ass off to hold a conversation with her. I just want something of ours, a kid and life of our own.”

Fuck her, anyone would be lucky to have Nicky as a kid.

Rio flew to the other side of the kitchen, dutifully standing at the waffle maker, scooping the batter.

They rolled their eyes, reaching into the cabinet and grabbing the damn chocolate chips. “How could I forget?”

“No,” They reached out, placing a hand on the small of her back and gently pushing her back the way she came. The shirt she had on was soft, and they could feel the warmth of her skin through it. “You just make it too strong.”

“Meh meh meh meh meh,” Agatha mocked in a high pitched voice, pouting as she slumped back into the stool. “I will spit it out if it doesn’t taste right.”

She could spit it in their face for all they cared…or mouth.

“I’d expect nothing less, mi amor.”

“Mija, we’re not flirting.”

Rio liked to think they were, but plausible deniability was useful.

“This would be a very poor excuse for flirting.” Agatha said, “You haven’t witnessed us in our prime.”

“Right.” Their daughter muttered, grabbing the coffee.

On their way out the door, they slid on a patch of ice, crashing backwards with their wife's hands shooting out to brace their fall. “Temps must've dropped last night, I’ll salt it when I get back.”

“Wanda mentioned that she was.”

She pursed her lips, shrugging. “It’s not like she really wants my input, she’s kind of anal about how she likes things. Nothing out of place, or not up to standard. She just…wants everything her way.”

Like she was waiting for Rio and Nicky to seem disappointed in her, spiteful even. But after yesterday, the fear melted, it had eased. She was proud. Proud of herself, and her daughter, and Rio. The vulnerability Rio put on display yesterday and today was jarring, but not necessarily in a bad way. They were doing better than ever, and it made Agatha want to do better.
