It’s all just Alex.

Agatha let the door swing open, the room looking no different. She apprehensively walked in, allowing her hand to brush along the crib as she did so. There’s nothing bad in here. The dust flurried up as a result, the particles shining in the light. The film covered her fingers, wiping the excess off on her jeans. Agatha exhaled, quietly backing out again. She left the door ajar on purpose, striding down the hall. It’s not so scary. And it wasn’t, not as much as before. If Nicky could find something redeemable about that room, then Agatha could too. It could be part of the house again, for the meantime.

It wasn’t that she didn’t believe Rio about Yelena or any potential women, she was fairly certain that her ex wouldn’t lure her into a false sense of security while at their daughter’s grave. It wasn’t that Rio wasn’t doing enough or not showing up. It wasn’t them, it was her. Agatha was, for all intents and purposes, basically a porcelain figure that had been shottily super glued back together over and over again for over forty years. Lilia, and Rio, and Nicky could only do so much, and Agatha didn’t want them to do more, that wasn’t their responsibility. She had to consider that ruminating in her pain would only amplify her darkest thoughts.

And there were a veritable fuckton of those, her lowest moment being right after Alex. Nobody knew about it and she didn’t plan on changing that, she didn’t need to be coddled. The grief and hopelessness were a drug that her brain had been simmering in for far too long, so, maybe she could improve? God, that sounded like so much work. But–

I wish you liked yourself the way you love me.

Kids say the darndest things.

Like words that haunt you even a day later, probably would until the day you die.

Agatha wished it too, honestly. If her daughter could recognize how low she felt, it was a sign clear as day that she needed to make a change. Alex’s room was a good way to start, leaving the door open, touching something. A goal could be walking in a little further each day, perhaps touching a different object. Who fucking knows, she was just throwing shit at the wall and seeing what stuck.

Wanda smiled brightly, grocery bags in her hands. “I don’t hate merlot.”

Agatha awkwardly chuckled, “Right.” Shit, she forgot that Wanda was coming back. She really had to stop doing that. “How much money did you spend at Whole Foods?”

Her girlfriend walked in, frazzled as stormed to the kitchen. “Not much, I thought we’d do breakfast for dinner. Sokovian tradition!”

She should’ve canceled this fucking dinner, along with the relationship. Agatha didn’t want to be alone, but at what fucking cost? She couldn’t do the babies and the cribs, she couldn’t imagine having more children. Alex was it, Nicky was more than enough. Agatha didn’t want kids with Wanda-

Holy shit, she didn’t want kids with Wanda.

“How European.” Agatha murmured, following. Nicky was already there, sketching with her headphones on at the island. “You cook? I’ve only ever heard you suggest Michelin star restaurants or takeout.”

Wanda let out a breath, exasperated. “I can make eggs and bacon.”

“Oh,” Nicky took off one ear of her headphones, setting down her pencil. “I’m suddenly vegan…sorry.”

Her girlfriend forced out a giggle, unpacking the groceries. “Spitfire, this one.”

“Kraft is formidable.” Nicky impassively commented.

“Rio’s coming?” Wanda cocked her head, tone shifting on a dime. “I didn’t know that.”

“It’s family dinner.” Nicky deadpanned. “You texted them about it.”

“I just thought that you had enough family time last night.” Wanda uttered, eye damn near twitching. “But that’s fine.”

The doorbell bellowed through the house, Agatha looking at her daughter. “Teddy, could you get that? It’s probably your mami with the wine. They might need some help if their hands are full.” Because who the fuck rang the doorbell anymore?

“Yeah.” Nicky said, slinging her headphones around her neck and hopping off the stool.

Agatha waited until Nicky was out of earshot before speaking to Wanda. “Are you doing all of this because of this morning?”

“What about this morning?” Wanda asked, pretending to be clueless.

“We’re not going to talk about it?”

“Talk about what?”

“You can’t just brush all of this aside.”

Wanda narrowed her gaze, titling her head, lethal in her response. “Can’t I?”

“Mama…?” Her daughter called out, confused and possibly put off.

Agatha put another pin that conversation, rushing to the foyer. As her sights focused, she was hit with a fucking tidal wave, and just as she was beginning to tread water.

“Who’s the hag?” Her daughter questioned, door wide open as a decrepit hand reached out to touch her.

“You’ve got quite the mouth,” A sinister voice stated, teeth bared in something close to a smile. “You know, I almost trained that out of my daughter.”

Agatha shot forward on instinct, practically flying the distance. “No!” She pulled Nicky by her shirt, akin to how a mama cat snatches up her kitten by the scruff, the outstretched hand falling short.

“Mom!” Nicky stumbled, her back softly hitting Agatha’s front. “What the hell? Who is that?”

Evanora viciously grinned, crossing the threshold into the house. “Your grandmother.”

Agatha steeled her grasp on Nicky, holding her daughter like something precious. And now, it made sense. The dinner and the stress. Agatha gritted her teeth, muttering under her breath “Wanda.”

They slowly backed away. “I’m good, I think…”

“Mami, it’s good for your pores.” Nicky wiggled the head band on them, pushing their hair back. “Just relax.”

“Apple cider vinegar,” their wife said. “It's a clay mask.”

Nicky giggled, but her face muscles didn’t really let her smile. “It means it’s gonna get really tight, really soon.”

“Do you both enjoy my suffering?” Rio accused, looking between their wife and daughter. “Is this fun for you?”

“A little bit,” Agatha snorted.

“Yup,” Nicky snickered.

And though Rio wouldn’t say it, a clay mask was a small price to pay for a night spent doing dumb stuff with their family. However, Nicky wasn’t lying, their face did feel really fucking tight after a few minutes. And they wouldn’t complain as Agatha curled against them with her head on their shoulder, they wouldn’t complain as their wife dozed off in the middle of the movie.

Rio didn’t complain once, not as they carried their wife to bed and said goodnight to their daughter and Scratchy. They couldn’t complain at all, because they finally had everything they ever wanted. They had their life back, and Rio wouldn’t take it for granted.

It was a little after 11PM when Rio roused to Agatha shaking them awake, her phone pressed to her ear as she frantically got up. She was pacing around, opening the closet and pulling out a sweater and jeans, nodding along. “Yeah, okay. Thank you.”

“What's up?” They rasped, trying to blink their eyes into working.

“I’ll be there as soon as possible.” Agatha hung up the phone, tears in her eyes. “That was the hospital, uh, my mom was in an accident.”

Rio scrambled out of bed. “Is she okay?!”

“I- I don’t know. They just called me because I’m her emergency contact but they didn’t tell me how she is.” She sniffled. “I guess she’s in the ER, so, um, I got to go.”

“Yeah, of course.” Rio grabbed a change of clothes. “I’ll get ready and then grab teddy.”

“You don’t have to do that.” Agatha’s words were weak, they were shaking. “It’s almost midnight-”

“I do,” Rio interrupted. “I do, because Lilia is my family because you’re my wife.” They hastily threw on some pants and a t-shirt. “Get dressed, I’ll get Nicky up, and I’ll drive. You just get yourself ready, okay?”

Agatha nodded, running her hands over her face to wipe the tears. “Okay.”

Rio kissed her temple, squeezing her hand. “I’m glad I stayed tonight.”

“Me too,” she whispered. “Thank you.”

“Whatever you need, baby,” Rio whispered back. “Gimme five minutes, and then we can go.”

Okay, so there was one thing to complain about.

The car wasn’t even fully in park before Rio’s wife bolted from the passenger’s seat, slamming the door and sprinting through the double doors of the ER. The drive to Mass Gen had been silent aside from Agatha’s quiet sniffles, a mirror of the morning Alex was born. Rio unbuckled their seatbelt, making sure Nicky was in tow before following after their wife. Their daughter was still in her hoodie in sweatpants, huge doe eyes already reddened from tears. Rio hadn’t let themself feel it yet, falling back into the role of being the strong one. Agatha needed them, and it wouldn’t do any good to fall apart right now, even if it felt like the world was collapsing in on itself.

Lilia was the only maternal figure in Rio’s life for a decade now, it didn’t matter if she didn’t give life to Rio, Lilia felt like their mother as much as Agatha’s. Rio found their wife at the front desk, frantically trying to find where her mom was located. They placed a hand on the small of her back as the overworked nurse clacked on her keyboard. “And your mom is Lilia Calderu?”

“Yes,” Agatha hissed. “Where is she?”

The nurse gave a weary smile. “It’ll be a minute before we take you back, have a seat.”

Agatha slammed her hands down on the desk. “You fucking listen-”

Rio snagged her arm, tugging her away. “Thank you.”

Their wife stared daggers at them as all three found seats in the waiting room. “Rio-”

“She’s got enough on her plate and nothing to gain from making us wait,” Rio stated. “Biting her head off won’t get you back there quicker, I promise you.”

“How long do you think it’ll be?” Nicky asked, slumping into a plastic chair.

“Few minutes,” they guessed. “They might need to finish some things up, or double check with nonna first, lots of things.”

Agatha’s knee bounced in the chair next to them. “Or she’s in worse shape than we thought and-”

Rio wrapped their fingers around her knee, squeezing to offer comfort. “We don’t know that yet.”

The time passed agonizingly slow, the minutes spanning what felt like hours. In reality, it couldn’t have been more than twenty before a social worker grabbed them, leading them into the back. Rio half shielded Nicky’s eyes as they passed by the patient bays, some more gruesome than others. There was already a doctor standing at the curtain, asking, “Calderu family?”

“Yes.” Agatha wiped her face, pointing to the curtain. “She in there?”

The doctor nodded. “Your mom-”

Agatha nudged him out of the way, frantically ripping the curtain open. “Mom?”

Lilia peered up from her Jello cup, eyes wide. “Hey guys!” She looked how she always did, hair pulled up haphazardly, oversized cardigan and palazzo pants on her frame—healthy as a fucking horse. “I can’t believe they called you, I told them not to.”

Rio could’ve sworn each one of them let out a simultaneous breath of relief.

Aagtha’s face fell in confusion, her mouth agape. “You- you look fine?”

“I am!” Lilia scraped at her Jello cup with a plastic spoon. “That’s what I kept saying.”

“It’s protocol when someone’s been in a wreck to have them checked out,” the doctor explained. “You mom doesn't have any contusions, everything came back clean, no speech or motor abnormalities.”

“Yeah!” Lilia hollered. “Because I’m fine!”

Agatha rounded her bed, taking a seat next to her and clasping Lilia’s hand in her own. “What happened?”

“Ah, some jackass ran a red.” She waved it off. “Clipped the front of my car.”

Lilia’s eyes flitted to Nicky, then to Rio. “I’m a woman of a certain age, I don’t have to defend late night visits to…gentleman callers.”

“What is wrong with this family,” Nicky whined under her breath.

Agatha actually chuckled. “You were going to a booty call?”

Rio grinned, patting their mother-in-law’s leg. “You scared us.”

“He’s a hot Italian man with all his real hair!” Lilia sat up, exaggerating with her hands. “I’ve endured a lot more for a lot less!”

“It very much was,” Lilia drawled. “Though, I will need a ride home.”

Agatha stood up, leaning down to throw her arms around her mom. “Don’t ever do that again. You are not allowed to die. Ever.”

“She does,” Rio ground out. “It’s just not her first language.”

Their brother chuckled under his breath. “Agatha speaks Spanglish.”

“He wanted to leave it to his son,” Isabella indelicately corrected. “Vic didn’t want it.”

“Damn thing doesn’t work anymore,” their brother muttered. “It’d just collect dust.”

Yes, she had agreed to play nice—but that was before they had made fun of her child and caused her boyfriend to cry. Real rich coming from the woman who disowned her own kid for no reason other than an insatiable need to demean the person you brought into this world!”

She was born into a good family, she was raised with everything made available to her and still—she ignored everything we gave her for a life in sin!”

Rio is compassionate, even when it’s hard to be. Rio is patient, and loving, and intelligent, and none of that is thanks to you! I have never, for even a second, questioned Rio’s character—I haven’t had to. You raised someone that other parents could only dream of, but because of the god you chose to serve, all of that is…?” She furrowed her brows and puckered her lips. “All of that is just bullshit?”

“You do not get to judge my life and parenting.” Isabella furiously waved her hand in punctuation. “Do you know what it feels like to create a child, nurture her, break your own body for her—and know she’ll never make it to heaven?”

Boy, did she.

“I would and have broken my body for my children. I’d give every ounce of blood, every pound of flesh, every modicum of breath if it meant my kid was okay. Your child is not a doll who lives and dies at your whim, you do not get to dictate who your child is! You do not get to demand Rio be miserable for your own selfish benefit! Rio does not exist so you sleep well at night! I can say without a single doubt that I’d sacrifice everything for my daughter…I have sacrificed everything for my daughter. As has Rio.” She looked her mother-in-law up and down. “And what kind of mother are you if you can’t say the fucking same?”

The face that closely resembled Rio’s turned vicious, Isabella roaring, “I will not be spoken to like this by a dyke who is raising a child she did not mother! You can live however you want, but do not bring it here! Your family is an abomination, and I have been nice enough to look the other way for decades, but I won’t do it anymore. Rio can pretend to be a man all she’d like, but not around me. Not around here. And certainly not today.”

I’ll let Rio know that we’re not welcome because their mother is bigoted cunt who cares more about a fake man in the sky than her own child. You won’t have to worry.” She sucked her teeth for a beat, cocking her head. “But when all your friends die out, and your judgement day comes and you're remembered by others with nothing but contempt—who do you want at your funeral, Isabella?” Her voice got low, lethally so. “‘Cause with the way you’re going, it’s just gonna be Vic and a paid-for priest.”

“Get out,” Isabella commanded. “Or I will throw you out myself.”

“My pleasure.” Agatha reached for the doorknob. “Fuck you, you made my husband cry, rot in hell.”

She left the coat check with several pairs staring at her, giving the small crowd a tiny salute as exit. Agatha walked back into the main atrium, her heels clacking along as she reached her daughter. Nicky’s arms were crossed as a few of Rio’s aunts surrounded her like crows picking at crumbs. “Do you have a boyfriend, Nicola?” One asked. Another giggling, “Are there any boys you like, at least?”

Nicky stared at them horrified, deadpanning, “Why would I like any boy ever?”

Agatha collected her daughter, smiling brightly as she said, “Ladies, please, we’ve already indoctrinated her.” And sauntered off with her arm around Nicky, both of them trying to suppress their laughter until they got outside. The win rapidly wore off as they reached Rio, leaning against the car with their palms in their eye sockets, bawling harder than Agatha had maybe ever witnessed. She let go of Nicky and unlocked the car, rushing over to them.

“Th- this was a mistake,” Rio blubbered, hunched over themself. “W- we shouldn’t have come. We shouldn’t have come. We shouldn’t h-have come!”

Agatha carefully removed their hands, bending down a little to get level with Rio. “Hey, hey,” she soothed, holding their face. “None of that was your fault, you did nothing wrong.”

“I let them down, all three of them. I let you and teddy down.” Rio’s voice was barely audible over their harsh sobs that sounded like their ribs hurt. “I- I let everyone down!”

“You didn’t let me down. You didn’t let teddy down either.” She ran her thumbs along their cheeks, trying to collect the tears. “Baby, we love you. What they think is their own cross to bear, it’s their loss.”

“Papá would be so disappointed in me, he d-didn't even mention me on his deathbed,” they hiccuped.

“Look at me,” Agatha whispered, waiting until reddened doe eyes locked onto hers. “You’re not a disappointment to us. You’re not wrong. You’re not living in sin. Rio, even on our worst days, you were still as compassionate and good as the day I met you. You are so good, my love. And I mean it this time—you have me and teddy, you always will, forever.”

They didn’t say anything more, merely collapsing in her embrace as their tears stained the fabric of her dress. Nicky came around the other side, hugging Rio as best she could. “We love you, mami. And those people were douchebags.”

Rio snorted at that, somewhere between weeping and laughing. “Thanks, mija.”

Agatha was able to herd both of them into the car, starting it and peeling the hell out of there. She wouldn’t actually tell Rio all that Isablla said, because she didn’t have the stomach to repeat it, and Rio definitely didn’t have the stomach to hear it. But that was okay, it was for the better. She’d be there for Rio to crumble, and she’d be there to help build them back up again.

Once they got home, Nicky chirped from the backseat, “You guys wanna know the good news, though?”

Rio gingerly swiveled their head to blink at her, rasping, “What?”

She dug in the pocket of her cardigan, holding up her hand with a familiar item clasped in her fingers. “I stole his watch.”

God help her, Agatha cackled, keeling over the steering wheel as Rio’s eyes widened to saucers. “Mi vida!” Rio squawked. “You robbed a corpse?!”

Nicky smirked. “It’s not like he fought back!”

Rio snatched the watch, running their thumb along the face of it. “Should we give it back?”

Agatha scowled. “Fuck no, our daughter robbed that corpse fair and square. You get what's yours, baby.”

They tentatively put it on, fastening the wristband and holding it out for Agatha and Nicky to see. “What do we think?”

She looked at them with so much love as she murmured, “So handsome.”

The rest of the night was spent slowly, lazily. Rio took their time, and Agatha didn’t rush them. Agatha whipped off her sleep shirt that night before bed, leaving her in just a pair of Rio’s boxers, the AC in their home was old and her hot flashes were too unbearable some days. Agatha sighed but she wouldn’t lie. “Yes.”

“And?” They appeared so hopeful, as if she’d say the perfect thing.

She pressed her lips together and gently shook her head.

Rio didn’t say anything, sitting with it. Then, “I get it now.”

“Get what?”

“I didn’t fight for you,” Rio uttered. “I never understood what that meant until today. You needed someone to fight for you when you couldn’t fight for yourself.” They brought their hand to her hair, playing with the ends. “You did that for me today, and I’m sorry I didn’t do that for you after Alex.”

“You fought for me every day since I told you that you could,” she said in return. “That’s not nothing.” Agatha smiled at them, pressing a soft kiss to their lips and snaking her arms around their shoulders, feeling a smile of their own.

They had passed the test. Rio’s grief wasn’t gone, but they could handle it together. They could handle the grief of Alex together—they had passed the fucking test. “Move back in,” Agatha proposed against their lips. “Fulltime.”

Rio relaxed against the pillow, resting their hold on the small of her back right before the swell of her ass, as they replied, “Well, considering our daughter is a kleptomaniac in the making-” Agatha let out an obnoxious snort-laugh before they finished. “Yeah, I think that’s a great idea, mi amor.”

“She’ll make an exceptional graverobber one day.”
